GT Equivalence Verification (BPG18)
============================================================
GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P
Candidate formulas: 85

GT (fixed function):
\[
0.4770530111687279\,P\sin(0.7760602430275763\,t)\;+\;0.44545499474048156(1-\tfrac{P}{51.06128580599878})P\;+\;0.44545499474048156P
\]
Expand the polynomial part:
\[
0.44545499474048156P - \frac{0.44545499474048156}{51.06128580599878}P^2 + 0.44545499474048156P
= 0.8909099894809631\,P - k\,P^2
\]
where \(k=\frac{0.44545499474048156}{51.06128580599878}\neq 0\).
So GT has exactly:
- a \(P\sin(\omega t)\) term with **zero phase shift** and \(\omega=0.7760602430...\),
- a **nonzero** \(P^2\) term,
- a **nonzero** linear \(P\) term,
- **no** other dependence on \(t\) (no standalone \(t\), no \(e^{t}\), etc.),
- **no** non-polynomial dependence on \(P\) (no \(\exp(P\cdot)\), \(\log\), \(|P|\), Max, etc.).

Below, each candidate can only match if all “extra structure” can be zeroed out and the remaining terms can reproduce \(-kP^2 + 0.89090998948P + 0.47705301117 P\sin(0.77606 t)\).

---

### 1.
Has \(P c3 e^{Pc4}\), \(c5 e^{Pc6}\), and \(c7 t^{c8}\). To match GT, must remove all these: set \(c3=0,c5=0,c7=0\). Remaining \(P c0\sin(c1 t + c2)\) lacks the required \(P^2\) and linear \(P\) terms. **No match.**

### 2.
Has \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\cos(c3 t+c4) + c5\sin(Pc6+c7)+c8\).
To remove \(\sin(P\cdot)\) set \(c5=0\); remove constant set \(c8=0\). But trig term is cosine, while GT needs sine. You could use \(\cos(x-\pi/2)=\sin(x)\), so cosine can represent sine by choosing phase \(c4=-\pi/2\) and \(c3=\omega\). Then \(Pc2\cos(c3 t+c4)=Pc2\sin(\omega t)\). Good.
Also can set \(c0=-k\), \(c1=0.89090998948...\), \(c2=0.47705301117...\), \(c3=0.7760602430...\), \(c4=-\pi/2\).
This seems promising—but note GT has **no constant term**, and we set \(c8=0\), fine. Also GT has no other \(P\)-dependence, and we set \(c5=0\), fine.
So candidate 2 **can** match GT.  
(Keep in mind cosine-to-sine via phase shift is valid for all \(t\).)

### 3.
Has \(P c4 e^{Pc5}\) plus \(c6 t + c7\). Must set \(c4=0,c6=0,c7=0\). Remaining \(Pc0 + Pc1\cos(c2 t+c3)\) has no \(P^2\) term. **No match.**

### 4.
Is \(P^2(c0+c1+c2)+P c3\sin(c4+c5 t)+Pc6\). This can represent \(P^2\) and \(P\sin(\omega t)\) and \(P\).
Choose \(c5=\omega\), \(c4=0\) to get \(\sin(\omega t)\) (phase 0), \(c3=0.477053...\), \(c6=0.890909...\), and \(c0+c1+c2=-k\).
All extra terms are already of allowed types. **Match possible.**

### 5.
\(P^2(c0+c1)+P c2\sin(c3 t+c4)+Pc5\). Same idea as (4) but fewer \(P^2\) coefficients.

### 6.

`0.4771*P*sin(0.7761*t) + 0.4455*P - 0.4455*P²/51.06 + 0.4455*P`
`= 0.4771*P*sin(0.7761*t) + 0.8909*P - 0.008726*P²`

So GT = **c_a*P² + c_b*P + c_c*P*sin(c_d*t)**

where c_a ≈ -0.008726, c_b ≈ 0.8909, c_c ≈ 0.4771, c_d ≈ 0.7761.

The GT has exactly three basis function terms: **P², P, P*sin(ωt)**.
